Chess
- I have always disliked playing chess
- The problem is that I don't like thinking
- The question: Do I like playing chess?
- I don't like the start, because I don't
know the starting positions
- I don't like loosing pieces.
- I don't like the time limit
- I hate the pawns.
- I don't like the end game, because I
don't know the ending moves
- I'm kind of a bad loser, because I focus
too much on myself ^IEpXyUba

Generalizing feelings from chess:
- Not having a clear understanding of
what is the goal
- Working under time pressure
- Needing to know something I
couldn't have or wouldn't need to
know
- Loosing ground, having an even
opponent
- Needing to use different level of
tools
 ^74UzQbag

Changing feelings
- Requires going to that feeling
- Figuring out what the feeling consist of
is done by making a statement or asking
a question from the subconsciousness,
like "I like public places."
- Being able to stay in there
- Start analyzing it
- Having a direction of how to change
the feeling
- Trying to feel how it would feel if being
in the goal
- Keep analyzing, understanding until
feeling the change
- There will be inner warnings that try to
sabotage this process. For example "I
have already done enough change".
- Even if the "conscious" mind says that
the feeling has been changed, the
subconscious feeling might still be there
intact. Do the process so long until you
feel the subconscious feeling being
changed. It can't be unnoticed. ^rOzcY8dt

KPOP
- My goal: Reduce the consumption of
kpop in my life and stop it being an
addiction.
- Statement: I will consume kpop max
30 minutes a day, and feel very little if
I were to not listen to it at all in one
week.
- The plan is to consume kpop max 30
minutes a day. Do I like it?
- Would I like to get rid of the habit?
From subconsciousness:
- I don't understand it.
- I feel the habit (triggers like eating). I
feel that nothing to replace watching
kpop comes to mind easily.
- I have felt being not that excited
watching kpop anymore, but continued
to do so just by habit
- I fear that kpop is too large source of
happiness to my life that I can't
decrease the amount of it.
- The idea of getting rid of the habit
does feel somewhat freeing. ^pHgvgTtx

Thoughts that came from
thinking about KPOP:

Being with my own mind

Where do I get happiness
from?

Slowing down my life
- Difficult, because I will need
to confront the reality more
- Most important moment to
remember this is between
tasks ^OUvUsgE5

Even if one trigger is removed, the other
triggers are still there. The brain doesn't
magically remove them, so take them into
consideration ^P6Qb2RJ3

- I'm someone who doesn't
like to prepare very much
- I'm very lazy to think
- I've done around 4000
hours worth of videos where
I just talk my thoughts aloud ^9Fc4MONF

thinking, I have pretty huge
barrier to seek information.

pretty naive ^6DXvGDKo
